Haimen: Autumn Harvest Assessment Set at 70% 110

This summer has been long and dry, and the crops have withered. The autumn harvest is less than 30%, making it the worst disaster in sixty years. Former County Magistrate Zhang reported this to the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Halls, which dispatched Ren Yingcang, Jiang Boru, and Wang Zhihong as autumn harvest assessment commissioners to Haimen to conduct a survey with Former County Magistrate Zhang. They then convened a meeting of representatives from various agencies and organizations to discuss the autumn harvest assessment. The three commissioners proposed 70%, but the representatives insisted that the maximum limit was 50%. The two sides argued for a long time, and the meeting ended without a result. The three commissioners still reported 70%, but the Finance Hall thought the number was too low and ordered the county to increase the levy as appropriate and wait for approval. Yesterday (the 15th), County Magistrate Chen notified various agencies and organizations that a meeting will be held this afternoon (the 16th) to discuss the matter. In addition, residents of the county, such as Zhang Chujiang, believe that the assessment set by the three commissioners is not based on the actual situation and violates the intention of the provincial halls to be mindful of the people's difficulties. Yesterday, they specially petitioned the provincial government and the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Halls to send officials to conduct a re-survey.

Large Quantity of Red Pills Seized 111

Qidong Chuanhonggang is located in a remote area along the river with a sparse population. Many drug dealers often hide there to manufacture and sell red pills to various townships in large quantities. The county government learned of this the day before yesterday and secretly ordered Xie Yun, the director of the police department, to lead more than a dozen policemen to arrest them. More than 1,000 red pills were seized in the Chen Yougen teahouse, and the drug dealer Chen Yougen was arrested and sent to the county government for interrogation.

Yangzhou: Envoy Miao's Coercion of the People Leads to Unrest 112

All sectors of Yangzhou have repeatedly petitioned for a delay in the relocation of the salt industry to the north, but have not been granted permission. Now, Envoy Miao arrived here from the province on the Zhenyang train at the Weishi hour on the 16th and entered the city to stay at the Deputy Salt Commissioner's Office. He first went to the Yangzhou Inspection Office to rest. The leaders of all sectors who were attending the county administrative meeting temporarily appointed Dai Tianqiu, Zhang Jichuan, Bao Xiangzhong, and Guo Lanshi as representatives to visit him at the office. However, the envoy's attitude was firm, and they did not get what they wanted. The joint association for maintaining the salt industry, in the name of the county party headquarters, convened an emergency meeting and decided to appoint Teng Yizhai, Han Guohua, Shi Ruizhan, Xi Kuishi, Ling Gengbo, and Qi Mingzhi as representatives to go to the Yangzhou Inspection Office Deputy's dormitory to petition the envoy. However, the guard at the dormitory, under orders, held a grenade launcher to intimidate them, refusing to let them enter. They waited outside the gate for a long time before the gate was opened and they were told to send representatives to meet the envoy. Teng and the other six representatives then submitted their calling cards and entered. However, Deputy Salt Commissioner Jin Xiangsheng met them instead, saying that it was mealtime and there were many female guests, so he had no time to meet them. He suggested that they wait or come back tomorrow. The representatives requested a meeting, but Jin said that it would be best to submit a written statement. The representatives then handed the petition to Jin to answer on his behalf. After a while, Jin came out and threw back the petition, saying that he would not meet them today or tomorrow. The representatives still tried to insist, but they were suddenly driven out by a police siren. Suddenly, dozens of armed tax police, carrying guns and ammunition, charged in with jeep-like vehicles. The petitioners fled in all directions. The dormitory lights went out at the same time. The tax police were stationed separately, and traffic was cut off, as if a major enemy had arrived. The envoy then returned to the Deputy Salt Commissioner's Office under armed escort. At 9:00 p.m., all sectors, angered by the envoy's arrogance, which was worse than that of a warlord, gathered at the Chamber of Commerce for an emergency meeting. They decided that the commercial, agricultural, educational, and automobile associations would jointly sign a telegram to County Magistrate Ma of the county government, stating that the relocation of the salt industry has caused panic throughout the county. Today, we were pleased to meet Envoy Miao Qiujie of Yangzhou. Representatives of all sectors of the people went to petition him, but Envoy Miao refused to meet them and ordered the tax police to threaten and expel them with guns, and mobilized a large number of tax police, carrying guns and ammunition, to charge at the people and order their arrest. Fortunately, they escaped quickly and avoided disaster. It is unbearable that he abuses his official power and uses violent means to deal with the people. The public is extremely angry and fears that an accident will occur. In addition to telegraphing the capital and provinces to send personnel to investigate and severely punish him, we hereby telegraph your government to protect the lives of the people and maintain public security, and simultaneously telegraph the Ministry of Finance, the Salt Administration, and the Executive Yuan. (The rest of the text is omitted.) It is also said that all sectors are extremely angry and declared a general strike of markets, classes, and workers on the 17th at the Chamber of Commerce meeting. If this is realized, traffic between Yangzhou and Zhenjiang will inevitably be cut off.

Ningbo: Elementary School Principal Commits Suicide After Losing Love 113

Chen Bofang, the 24-year-old principal of Hanxia Baocui Elementary School in the Fourth District of Yuyao, suffered a sudden mental breakdown last year due to the stimulus of losing love. He disappeared once in July. Later, his family and others brought him back and kept him at home. This autumn, because he was a little more stable, the surveillance was relaxed. Unexpectedly, he suddenly ran away again on the 8th of this month. His family was panicked and searched everywhere without a trace. Until yesterday (the 15th), his body was suddenly found in the river near Yitaishan Temple. Yang Jinshun, a constable from Gaoyi Township Office, pulled the body ashore and immediately reported it to his sister, Ms. Chen Guanying, who identified it and made arrangements for the coffin.

Special Report

The Constitution of the Republic of China Passed by the Legislative Yuan in the Third Reading (Continued) 114

Chapter IV: The Central Government

Section 1: The President

Article 36: The President is the head of state and represents the Republic of China externally.

Article 37: The President promulgates laws and issues orders in accordance with the law, and these must be countersigned by the heads of the relevant Yuan.

Article 38: The President commands the national army, navy, and air force in accordance with the law.

Article 39: The President exercises the power to declare war, negotiate peace, and conclude treaties in accordance with the law.

Article 40: The President declares and lifts martial law in accordance with the law.

Article 41: The President exercises the power to grant amnesties, special pardons, commutations of sentences, and restoration of rights in accordance with the law.

Article 42: The President appoints and removes civil and military officials in accordance with the law.

Article 43: The President confers honors in accordance with the law.

Article 44: The President oversees the administration.

Article 45: The President is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 46: Citizens of the Republic of China who are forty years of age or older may be elected as President or Vice President.

Article 47: Military personnel may not be elected as President or Vice President unless they have been discharged from their duties.

Article 48: The election of the President and Vice President shall be determined by law.

Article 49: The terms of office for the President and Vice President are both four years, and they may be re-elected for one consecutive term.

Article 50: The President shall take an oath on the day of assuming office. The oath reads as follows: "I solemnly swear to the people with a sincere and earnest heart that I will abide by the Constitution, be loyal to my duties, promote the welfare of the people, defend the country, and not fail the trust of the people. If I violate this oath, I am willing to be subject to the severe sanctions of the national law. I solemnly swear."

Article 51: If the President is unable to perform their duties due to circumstances, the Vice President shall act on their behalf. If both the President and Vice President are unable to perform their duties, the President of the Executive Yuan shall act on their behalf.

Article 52: The President shall be relieved of their duties on the day their term expires. If the next President has not yet been elected by the expiration date, or if neither the elected President nor Vice President has assumed office, the President of the Executive Yuan shall act as President.

Article 53: The term for which the President of the Executive Yuan acts as President shall not exceed six months.

Article 54: Except in cases of treason or insurrection, the President shall not be subject to criminal prosecution unless impeached or dismissed.

Section 2: The Executive Yuan

Article 55: The Executive Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising administrative power.

Article 56: The Executive Yuan shall have one President and twenty Ministers without Portfolio, who shall be appointed and removed by the President.

Article 57: The Executive Yuan shall establish various ministries and commissions to manage administrative functions.

Article 58: The ministers of the various ministries and the chairpersons of the various commissions of the Executive Yuan shall be appointed and removed by the President from among the Ministers without Portfolio.

Article 59: The President of the Executive Yuan, the Ministers without Portfolio, the ministers of the various ministries, and the chairpersons of the various commissions shall each be responsible to the President.

Article 60: The Executive Yuan shall establish an Executive Council, composed of the President, the President of the Executive Yuan, and the Ministers without Portfolio. The President shall be the chairperson. If the President is unable to attend due to circumstances, the President of the Executive Yuan shall be the chairperson.

Article 61: The following matters shall be decided by the Executive Council: (1) Bills and budget proposals submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (2) Proposals for martial law and amnesties submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (3) Proposals for declarations of war, peace treaties, treaty proposals, and other proposals regarding important international matters submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (4) Matters of common concern among the various ministries and commissions; (5) Matters referred to the Council by the President; (6) Matters proposed by the President of the Executive Yuan, the Ministers without Portfolio, the ministers of the various ministries, and the chairpersons of the various committees.

Article 62: The organization of the Executive Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section 3: The Legislative Yuan

Article 63: Legislative Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising legislative power and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 64: The Legislative Yuan has the power to decide on legislative bills, martial law, amnesties, declarations of war, peace treaties, treaty proposals, and other matters concerning important international affairs.

Article 65: Regarding legislative matters, the Legislative Yuan may pose questions to the various Yuan, ministries, and commissions.

Article 66: The Legislative Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, who may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 67: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Legislative Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the legislators shall mutually elect an acting president.

Article 68: Legislators shall be elected in accordance with the following regulations:

(1) National representatives elected from various provinces, Mongolia, Tibet, and overseas Chinese citizens shall hold preliminary elections. Candidate lists shall be submitted to the National Assembly for election according to the following quotas. The candidates are not limited to national representatives: (a) For provinces with a population of less than 5 million, three representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 5 million or more but less than 10 million, four representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 10 million or more but less than 15 million, five representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 15 million or more but less than 20 million, six representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 20 million or more but less than 25 million, seven representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 25 million or more but less than 30 million, eight representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 30 million or more but less than 35 million, nine representatives per province; for provinces with a population of 35 million or more, ten representatives per province; (b) Six representatives each for Mongolia and Tibet; (c) Six representatives for overseas Chinese citizens. (2) The President of the Legislative Yuan shall select individuals with specialized knowledge and experience and submit a list of candidates to the National Assembly for election. The number of candidates shall not exceed one-third of the total number in the previous clause.

Article 69: Legislators shall serve a term of four years and may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 70: The Executive Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Examination Yuan, and Control Yuan may submit proposals to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under their jurisdiction.

Article 71: The President may, prior to the promulgation or implementation of a resolution passed by the Legislative Yuan, submit it for reconsideration. If the Legislative Yuan, upon reconsideration of the aforementioned proposal, upholds the original decision by a two-thirds majority of the members present, the President shall immediately promulgate or implement it.

Article 72: The President shall promulgate a resolution passed by the Legislative Yuan within thirty days of its receipt.

Article 73: Legislators shall not be held responsible externally for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 74: Except in cases of flagrant offense, legislators may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Legislative Yuan.

Article 75: Legislators may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 76: The election of legislators and the organization of the Legislative Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section 4: The Judiciary Yuan

Article 77: The Judicial Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising judicial power, in charge of civil, criminal, and administrative litigation trials, disciplinary actions against civil servants, and judicial administration.

Article 78: The Judicial Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, who shall be appointed by the President with the consent of the Legislative Yuan. The President of the Judicial Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 79: The Judicial Yuan shall establish a Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions of Public Functionaries and a Ministry of Judicial Administration.

Article 80: The chairperson and members of the Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions of Public Functionaries and the minister of the Ministry of Judicial Administration shall be nominated by the President of the Judicial Yuan in accordance with the law and submitted to the President for appointment and removal.

Article 81: Matters concerning amnesty, commutation of sentence, and restoration of rights shall be submitted by the President of the Judicial Yuan to the President for execution in accordance with the law.

Article 82: The Judicial Yuan has the power to interpret laws and orders uniformly.

Article 83: Judges shall conduct trials independently in accordance with the law.

Article 84: Judges shall not be dismissed unless they are subject to criminal penalties or disciplinary sanctions, or declared legally incompetent. They shall not be suspended, transferred, or have their salaries reduced without legal basis.

Article 85: The organization of the Judicial Yuan and the organization of courts at all levels shall be determined by law.

Section 5: The Examination Yuan

Article 86: The Examination Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising the power of examination, in charge of examinations and personnel assessment.

Article 87: The Examination Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, who shall be appointed by the President with the consent of the Legislative Yuan. The President of the Examination Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 88: The Examination Yuan shall establish a Ministry of Personnel and a Board of Examiners when examinations are held.

Article 89: The minister of the Ministry of Personnel shall be nominated by the President of the Examination Yuan in accordance with the law and submitted to the President for appointment and removal.

Article 90: The following qualifications shall be determined through examinations and assessments by the Examination Yuan in accordance with the law: (1) Qualifications for appointment of civil servants; (2) Qualifications of candidates for public office.

Article 91: The organization of the Examination Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section 6: The Control Yuan

Article 92: The Control Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising the power of supervision, in charge of impeachment and auditing, and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 93: In order to exercise its power of supervision, the Control Yuan may pose questions to the various Yuan, ministries, and commissions in accordance with the law.

Article 94: The Control Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, who may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 95: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Control Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the members of the Control Yuan shall mutually elect an acting president.

Article 96: Members of the Control Yuan shall be nominated by two national representatives pre-selected from each province, Mongolia, Tibet, and overseas Chinese citizens, and submitted to the National Assembly for election. The candidates are not limited to national representatives.

Article 97: Members of the Control Yuan shall serve a term of four years and may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 98: When central and local government officials violate the law or neglect their duties, the Control Yuan, upon the proposal of one or more members of the Control Yuan and the review and decision of five or more members, may file an impeachment case. However, impeachment cases against the President, Vice President, and the Presidents of the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Examination Yuan, and Control Yuan must be proposed by ten or more members of the Control Yuan and decided by a review of one-half or more of all members of the Control Yuan before they can be filed.

Article 99: Impeachment cases shall be submitted to the Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions of Public Functionaries, unless otherwise specified in the Constitution as to the receiving authority.

When the Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions of Public Functionaries decides that an impeached person should be dismissed or subjected to other disciplinary actions, the President or the responsible superior shall implement the decision.

Article 100: Impeachment cases against the President, Vice President, and the Presidents of the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Examination Yuan, and Control Yuan, after being established in accordance with the provisions of Article 98, shall be submitted to the National Assembly. During the adjournment of the National Assembly, a temporary National Assembly shall be convened by the National Representatives in accordance with the law to decide whether or not to remove them from office.

Article 101: The Control Yuan shall establish an Auditing Committee to manage auditing affairs.

Article 102: The chairperson and members of the Auditing Committee shall be nominated by the President of the Control Yuan in accordance with the law and submitted to the President for appointment and removal.

Article 103: The Auditing Committee's final accounts report, after being reviewed by the Control Yuan meeting, shall be promulgated in accordance with the law.

Article 104: Members of the Control Yuan shall not be held responsible externally for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 105: Except in cases of flagrant offense, members of the Control Yuan may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Control Yuan.

Article 106: Members of the Control Yuan may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 107: The election of members of the Control Yuan and the organization of the Control Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter V: Province

Article 108: Provinces shall establish provincial governments to implement central laws and supervise local autonomy.

Article 109: Provincial governments shall have one governor, with a term of three years, who shall be appointed and removed by the central government. Military personnel may not be appointed as governor unless they have been discharged from their duties for three years.

Article 110: Provinces shall establish provincial assemblies. The number of councilors shall be one per county or city, elected by the county and city councils. The term of office is three years, and they may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 111: Provincial assemblies shall meet once a year for a session not exceeding one month. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary.

Article 112: The functions and powers of the Provincial Assembly are as follows: (1) To deliberate and resolve on the provincial government's budget submitted to the central government; (2) To submit legislative matters concerning the province to the Legislative Yuan; (3) To deliberate and resolve on single regulations delegated by law; (4) To submit proposals to the Executive Yuan regarding the development and reform of provincial administration; (5) To submit proposals to the Control Yuan regarding the impeachment of provincial government officials; (6) To deliberate and resolve on matters referred to the Council by the provincial governor; (7) To make recommendations to the provincial governor.

Article 113: The organization of the provincial government, the organization of the provincial assembly, and the election and recall of provincial councilors shall be determined by law.

Article 114: The political system for areas where provinces have not been established shall be determined by law.

Chapter VI: County

Article 115: The county is a unit of local self-government.

Article 116: Matters of county self-government are as follows: (1) Investigation and registration of county household registration; (2) County land administration matters; (3) County financial matters; (4) County transportation, water conservancy, and other engineering construction matters; (5) County public and cooperative matters; (6) County security and public order matters; (7) County education and culture matters; (8) County health matters; (9) County conservation and relief matters; (10) Custody and management of county public property; (11) Preservation of county scenic spots and historical sites; (12) Other matters belonging to county self-government.

Article 117: County residents shall exercise the rights of initiative and referendum regarding county self-government matters in accordance with the law, and exercise the rights of election and recall of the county magistrate and other county self-government personnel in accordance with the law.

Article 118: Counties shall establish county councils. Councilors shall be elected by the county residents' assembly for a term of three years and may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Article 119: County councils shall meet twice a year for a session not exceeding one month. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary.

Article 120: The functions and powers of the county council are as follows: (1) To deliberate and resolve on the county budget and review county final accounts; (2) To deliberate and resolve on county taxes and contracts that increase the county treasury's burden; (3) To deliberate and resolve on the management and disposal of county property; (4) To audit county finances; (5) To deliberate and resolve on county single regulations; (6) To recommend county administrative reforms to the county government; (7) To deliberate and resolve on matters referred to the Council by the county magistrate; (8) To question the county magistrate on matters.

Article 121: County single regulations that conflict with central laws or provincial regulations are invalid.

Article 122: Counties shall establish county governments, with one county magistrate, who shall be elected by the county residents' assembly for a term of three years and may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Candidates for county magistrate shall be limited to those who have passed the central examination or assessment.

Article 123: The county magistrate shall handle county self-government matters and be subject to the direction of the provincial governor in implementing matters entrusted by the central government and the province.

Article 124: The organization of the county council, the election and recall of county councilors, the organization of the county government, and the election and recall of the county magistrate shall be determined by law.

Chapter VII: City

Article 125: The self-government and administration of cities shall apply mutatis mutandis to the provisions concerning counties, unless otherwise provided by law.

Article 126: Cities shall establish city councils. Councilors shall be elected by the city residents' assembly, with one-third of the members being re-elected each year.

Article 127: Cities shall establish city governments, with one mayor, who shall be elected by the city residents' assembly for a term of three years and may be re-elected for consecutive terms.

Candidates for mayor shall be limited to those who have passed the central examination or assessment.

Article 128: The mayor shall handle city self-government matters and be subject to the direction of the supervisory authority in implementing matters entrusted by the central government or the province.

Article 129: The organization of the city council, the election and recall of city councilors, the organization of the city government, and the election and recall of the mayor shall be determined by law.

Chapter VIII: National Economy

Article 130: The economic system of the Republic of China shall be based on the Principle of People's Livelihood to ensure an equitable distribution of livelihood for all citizens.

Article 131: Land within the territory of the Republic of China belongs to the entire people. Land owned by the people in accordance with the law shall have its ownership protected and restricted by law. The state may levy taxes or requisition land owned by the people in accordance with the land price declared by the landowner or assessed by the government in accordance with the law.

Landowners are obligated to make full use of their land.

Article 132: Minerals attached to the land and natural forces that can be used economically by the public belong to the state and are not affected by the people's acquisition of land ownership.

Article 133: Land value that increases not due to labor or capital input shall be collected for public enjoyment through the levy of land value increment tax.

Article 134: The state's distribution and reorganization of land shall be based on the principle of supporting independent farmers and those who use the land themselves.

Article 135: If the state believes that private wealth and private enterprises hinder the balanced development of the people's livelihood, it may restrict them in accordance with the law.

Article 136: The state shall encourage, guide, and protect national production enterprises and foreign trade.

Article 137: Public utilities and other monopolistic enterprises shall be operated by the state in principle. However, private operation by citizens may be specially licensed if necessary. The state may temporarily manage privately operated enterprises licensed in the preceding paragraph due to urgent national defense needs, and may take them over for public operation in accordance with the law, but appropriate compensation shall be given.

Article 138: The state shall implement a labor protection policy to improve workers' lives, increase their productive skills, and provide relief for unemployed workers. Women and children engaged in labor shall be given special protection according to their age and physical condition.

Article 139: Labor and capital shall develop production enterprises based on the principle of coordination and mutual assistance.

Article 140: In order to promote agricultural development and the welfare of farmers, the state shall enrich the rural economy, improve rural life, and improve farmers' farming efficiency through scientific methods. The state may regulate the types, quantities, and distribution of agricultural products.

Article 141: The state shall provide appropriate relief or pensions to people who become disabled or die due to military service or public duties.

Article 142: The state shall provide appropriate relief to the elderly, weak, disabled, and those unable to live. (To be continued)

Local News

Kong Xiangxi Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 115

Talks about the gradual stabilization of domestic finance

According to the Central News Agency, Kong Xiangxi, Deputy President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, left Nanjing by overnight train the night before last at 11:00 PM and arrived at Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:15 AM. He got off at the Zhenru station and went directly to his private residence on Avenue Road. He then went to the Central Bank on the Bund at around 10:00 AM to handle bank affairs. Kong met with reporters from various newspapers yesterday. According to him, since the implementation of the increased silver export tax, it has been sufficient to prevent the rampant outflow of silver, and domestic finance is gradually stabilizing. There is currently no need to take other measures. Regarding the issue of currency system reorganization, the Currency System Reorganization Committee has been studying the methods in detail, and implementation will begin as soon as a decision is made. Lu Xuepu, director of the Central Mint, previously submitted his resignation due to physical weakness and difficulty in managing the factory's affairs. After being retained, he is now seeking to resign again. He is currently being retained. As for the accounting conference held in Nanjing this time, it is to discuss methods for improving and unifying accounting.

He Yingqin Visited Old Friends Yesterday 116

And received former subordinates at his residence

He Yingqin, Minister of Military Administration and Acting Chairman of the Peiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission, arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing the day before yesterday morning. Yesterday, in addition to receiving former subordinates at his residence, he also went out by car with his secretary Xie Zhongyuan, his adjutant Wang Guozhong, and others to visit old friends in Shanghai. Mayor Wu Tiecheng plans to host a banquet in the next few days to welcome He, but the date has not yet been decided.

Gu Xinyi Urges the Ministry of Finance to Amend the Stamp Tax Law 117

Gu Xinyi, chairman of the Shanghai Soybean and Rice Industry Association, telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying: "To Minister Kong of the Nanjing Ministry of Finance, Recently, it has been reported that the Legislative Yuan has drafted a stamp tax law. Article 16 lists that 1. invoices, 2. receipts for money and goods, 3. bills, all with an amount of three yuan or more, will have a stamp of one cent affixed for every ten yuan. Regarding the one-cent stamp starting at three yuan, your consideration of the merchants' difficulties is deeply appreciated. However, with respect to affixing a one-cent stamp for every ten yuan, this treats these extremely common, very minor rights, short-term proofs as goods of value and imposes a progressive heavy tax, which is many times, even dozens of times, higher than the tax rate of the current provisional stamp tax regulations promulgated by your ministry. This differs greatly and is clearly inconsistent with Article 5 of the principles of the Stamp Tax Law established by the Central Political Conference last year, which states that lighter taxation should be applied to proofs with minor validity or rights, or short usage periods, and Article 6, which states that fixed tax rates should be adopted for proofs of frequent actions. This will only lead to the decline of all industries, the withering of the market, and the extreme plight of merchants. Having heard that the government is vigorously abolishing harsh and miscellaneous taxes, we were deeply gratified, believing that there was hope for recovery. Unexpectedly, the stamp tax law drafted by the Legislative Yuan imposes a progressive tax on the above-mentioned proofs that are used daily in the market, which is similar to a harsh and miscellaneous tax. Not only is it impossible for merchants to bear this after their exhaustion, but it also seems difficult for the government's credibility to be enforced. Therefore, I dare to telegraph you and request that you review it and forward it to the Executive Yuan, which will consult the Legislative Yuan and earnestly request that it be revised again in accordance with the principles established by the Central Political Conference last year, in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and facilitate implementation. I am overwhelmed with eagerness and trepidation. Respectfully, Gu Xinyi, chairman of the Shanghai Soybean and Rice Industry Association."

Jiaxu Disaster Relief Association Raises Large Funds to Purchase 100,000 Shi of Foreign Rice 124

For Winter and Spring Relief Needs

Requests Authorities to Issue Tax-Exempt Passports

The Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, in order to prepare and advance large sums of money, is sending personnel to various locations such as Nanyang, Siam, and Java to purchase 100,000 shi of relief rice. This rice will be shipped in batches to Shanghai and then transported to the interior to provide winter relief. The association yesterday sent a special telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting that they forward a request to the Ministry of Finance to issue tax-exempt passports in order to benefit the disaster victims. Additionally, letters and telegrams have been sent to various organizations across the country soliciting aid. Details are as follows:

Banking Sector Suggests Forming a Silver Price Stabilization Committee 125

And is Willing to Have Each Bank Contribute to its Fund

The Ministry of Finance is Currently Studying and Considering the Proposal

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the increased silver export tax, and based on the London silver price, converted to the Shanghai exchange rate, the difference between this exchange rate and the exchange rate determined by the Central Bank on that day, after paying the export tax, is still insufficient. In such cases, a balancing tax is levied based on the amount of the deficiency, which is announced daily by the Central Bank at 11:30 AM. To stabilize silver prices, the Ministry of Finance is planning to establish a silver price stabilization committee. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency learned from the banking sector yesterday that the proposal to establish the silver price stabilization committee was made by the banking sector to the Ministry of Finance. Minister Kong Xiangxi is currently considering and studying this proposal. It is understood that various countries in Europe and America have organizations for price stabilization committees and have a large amount of funds for balancing foreign exchange. The proposal from our country's banking sector is also based on the methods of various countries. It is rumored that if the Ministry of Finance approves the establishment, banks such as the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications will be responsible for its funding.

(Standing Committee Meeting) The association held its fifth regular standing committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM at its meeting place. Over thirty people attended, including Chu Huiseng, Yu Zhongxian, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Shenzhi, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, etc. Chu Huiseng presided over the meeting, Chen Weixuan recorded the proceedings. After the chairman reported on the letters and telegrams requesting aid from Lin'an, Xinchang, Jiangshan, Yuqian, Tonglu, Chongde, Changxing, and other places, the following proposals were discussed. Qu Wenliu proposed the issue of whether to send people to investigate the disaster situation in various counties and how to allocate the advance funds for relief. It was resolved to consult with the Zhejiang Relief Association to determine the severity of the disaster and each identify areas for relief and distribute aid separately. The method for distributing advance funds was to allocate 5,000 yuan to the counties with the most severe disasters, 4,000 yuan to those with the next most severe, and 3,000 yuan to those with the third most severe. A total of 100,000 yuan was temporarily allocated for emergency relief. Chairman Chu Huiseng was recommended to go to Hangzhou to negotiate with the Provincial Government. Over ten investigators were also dispatched to carry report forms and inspect the disaster situation in various counties. The meeting adjourned at approximately 6:00 PM.

(Submission to Zhejiang Provincial Government) The association submitted a document to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, stating: "To the esteemed Zhejiang Provincial Government, this year's drought in Zhejiang Province has resulted in a disaster, with the autumn harvest of fields and crops being hopeless. According to the investigation report of the National Government Relief Committee, the disaster-stricken area covers 70 counties and one city in the entire province. The coastal and mountainous rural areas, in particular, have suffered a complete crop failure. Just as new grains are entering the market, rice prices continue to rise incessantly, making the situation even more unimaginable by the time the green and yellow crops are out of season next spring. Zhejiang Province's rice production is inherently insufficient, and it has relied on commercial transportation from other provinces such as Xichang, Xiang, and Gan for many years. Now, all regions are suffering from drought, and the source of supply is about to dry up, making the food situation for the people all the more worrying. Our association has repeatedly convened meetings and plans to raise a large sum of money to purchase 100,000 shi of relief grain from Nanyang, Siam, Java, and other places, and ship them in batches to Shanghai for transportation to the counties most severely affected by the disaster in the interior for winter and spring relief. However, to reduce transportation costs and save relief funds, we earnestly request that you forward our request to the Ministry of Finance, examine and follow the regulations on tax exemption for disaster relief goods, and approve an official order to the Customs Administration and the Shanghai Customs to exempt the import tax on this relief grain, in order to benefit the impoverished people and emphasize the importance of disaster relief. If approved, we will prepare a detailed list of tax-exempt passport requests for relief grain and submit it for forwarding and approval. This case concerns the purchase of a large amount of grain, so we earnestly request you to examine and approve it promptly. This is for the public convenience. Sincerely, the Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, Xiao."

(Telegram Soliciting Aid) The association sent a letter and telegram to various organizations across the country yesterday, soliciting aid, stating: "This year's drought in Zhejiang has resulted in a disaster. From summer to autumn, it has not rained for a hundred days, and the number of affected counties has reached as many as sixty-nine. Fields and crops have withered, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. In addition to the years of consecutive crop failures, the entire region has suffered a common calamity. Starving people are crying out, anxiously awaiting food. We have now gathered colleagues from inside and outside the province to establish the Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, using the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai on Tibet Road as the meeting place. We have published donation appeals and are assigning responsibilities for soliciting donations. We humbly hope that renowned figures and prominent figures in our hometowns will have compassion for this great calamity and generously contribute to our cause. Every penny and ounce is welcome, and no amount is too large. More relief funds mean more lives saved. Millions of disaster victims are waiting with outstretched necks. Your lofty friendship is no different from experiencing it ourselves. Honorary Chairmen: Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Song Hanzhang; Chairmen: Chu Huiseng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai; Director of General Affairs Group: Zhang Shenzhi; Deputy Directors: Cha Zhongjian, Zhuang Yuqing; Director of Donation Affairs Group: Du Yuesheng; Deputy Directors: Kui Yanfang, Zhang Weiru; Director of Finance Group: Xu Jiying; Deputy Directors: Xu Yushu, Pei Yunqing; Director of Relief Affairs Group: Qu Wenliu; Deputy Directors: Yin Zhufu, Fan Zhenchu."

Sichuan Exchange Rate Soars; Sichuan Merchants Suspend Purchasing Shanghai Goods 126

Since the beginning of this year, a large amount of cash from Sichuan Province, totaling 20 million yuan, has been successively remitted to Shanghai, causing the exchange rate between Chongqing and Wanxian to rise to a maximum of 1,370 yuan to equal 1,000 Shanghai dollars. Subsequently, the Sichuan provincial authorities restricted the exchange rate to no more than 1,250 yuan, but in reality, this had no effect. The exchange rate continued to soar, increasing even more drastically in recent days, reaching over 1,400 yuan yesterday, creating a new record since the Republic of China. Sichuan merchants primarily purchased cotton yarn and, to a lesser extent, general merchandise from Shanghai. Since the exchange rate has risen sharply, the cost of purchasing Shanghai goods has increased by 40%, so they have all telegraphed Shanghai to suspend purchases.

(Two) Division Commander Li Jueyu of the Hunan Army (6th) arrived at Baisha in Shiqian. The throat of Wujiang is secretly guarded by the 囗囗囗 troops at night. Army Commander Wang Jialie personally supervised his troops in day and night pursuit and suppression, killing many bandits in recent days. Director of the National Bureau of Weights and Measures, Wu Chengluo, Left Shanghai for Hong Kong Yesterday 132

To Inspect Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Fujian

Since Wu Chengluo (Zi Jiandong) took charge of the Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industries, the promotion of weights and measures administration has been quite effective. Recently, Mr. Wu, in view of the fact that the new system has gradually become widespread in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, Shandong, and Hebei, decided to personally inspect the situation in the provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Fujian to thoroughly understand the national promotion. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, he boarded the Jefferson of the Da Lai Company for Hong Kong, and then went to the provinces of Guangdong and Guangxi. Many people from the academic and engineering circles of this city accompanied him. A reporter from the Datong News Agency met Mr. Wu on the ship and recorded his conversation as follows: According to Mr. Wu, regarding the standardization of weights and measures throughout the country, the central government believes that this is the foundation of economic and social construction, and also the first step towards rationalizing industry. Therefore, it is determined to complete the work in the shortest possible time, that is, to implement standardization before the end of political tutelage and the beginning of constitutional government. The degree of progress can now be said to be consistent throughout the country. In the provinces along the Yangtze River and the coast, the standardization work has spread from cities to villages due to convenient transportation. Even in the northwest, which is located on the frontier, they are actively engaged in this work. In recent years, in addition to adhering to the guidelines of the Ministry in the central government and engaging in measures for weights and measures administration, the manufacture of standards, and the training of inspection specialists, I have also regularly gone to various provinces, cities, and counties in stages, in order to contribute to the local areas. The local areas' eagerness to expect weights and measures administration is sometimes even greater than that of the central government. The actual work of standardization truly relies on the perseverance of local officials and the sincere acceptance of local industrial and academic circles. The southwestern provinces are also carrying out this administration with great intensity, which is a blessing for the entire political unity of our country. This time, I was ordered by the government to go to Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Fujian provinces for inspection. In addition to weights and measures administration, I also plan to conduct a detailed investigation of industrial construction. The southwest has a whole step and solid advancement for the construction of industrial production, and its effects can also be used as a reference for the central government's policy implementation and a model for other provinces. In addition, the central government takes weights and measures as the basis, and then seeks to formulate and implement standard specifications for various agricultural and industrial industries. These standards should conform to scientific theory on the one hand, and also refer to the habits of our country on the other hand. Therefore, the established rules of various industries in the southwest are also included in the investigation, etc.

Jiangsu Provincial Government and Jin Cheng and Other Banks Jointly Operate Small-Scale Loans for Common People 135

Jin Cheng 50,000, Farmers of Jiangsu 25,000 Each

Provincial Government Guarantees 5% Interest and Bears Full Responsibility for Compensation

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, in order to relieve unemployed common people, the Jiangsu Provincial Government contacted Jin Cheng and three other banks to issue 100,000 yuan for small-scale loans to common people, and decided to first conduct a trial in Zhenjiang. The details are as follows:

(Negotiations Completed) In view of the decline of the rural areas, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, in order to relieve the common people, planned to establish a Small-Scale Loan Office for Common People. The loan fund has been contacted by Zhao Dihua, Director of the Finance Department, with Jin Cheng, Jiangsu, and Farmers banks to jointly undertake 100,000 yuan for operation. The provincial government will provide a 5% interest guarantee and bear full responsibility for compensation. Negotiations have been completed. It is estimated that Jin Cheng Bank will undertake 50,000 yuan, and Jiangsu and Farmers banks will each undertake 25,000 yuan, totaling 100,000 yuan.

(About to Start Trial) The Jiangsu Provincial Government will implement small-scale loans for common people after signing a contract with Jin Cheng and three other banks. It has also decided to first conduct a trial in Zhenjiang. If it is successful, it will then expand and popularize it in various counties. It is heard that the amount of the loan requested by common people is stipulated to be from 5 yuan to 20 yuan, with a term of six months, repaid in installments, with an interest rate of 8%, and a Small-Scale Loan Office for Common People will be established first, which will be handled by personnel sent by the provincial government.

Chairman Chen of Jiangsu Provincial Government Plans to Borrow 1 Million from the Boxer Indemnity Fund 136

For the Development of Fisheries

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, Chen Guofu, Chairman of Jiangsu Province, believes that the length of our coastal fishing area is unmatched by other countries, but fishermen are unable to develop due to economic limitations. He has prepared a detailed plan and submitted it to the Executive Yuan and Chairman Chiang to borrow 1 million from the Boxer Indemnity Committee to purchase four new-style fishing vessels for exclusive deep-sea fishing. A reporter has obtained the detailed plan, excerpts from which are as follows:

Perfect Equipment for All Parts of the Ship 137

In order to develop the deep-sea fishing grounds of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, Chairman Chen has prepared a plan to borrow 1 million from the British Boxer Indemnity Committee to purchase four new-style steel trawler fishing vessels. The ship is 140 feet long, 24.5 feet wide, and 13.5 feet deep, with an average draft of 14.5 feet, weighing approximately 350 tons. It is equipped with a triple expansion steam engine, approximately 600 horsepower, 1254 revolutions per minute, and a speed of 11 knots. The coal capacity is 200 tons, which can carry 60 tons of ice and 40 tons of water. The fish hold has perfect equipment, as well as wireless communication reaching 250 nautical miles, and crew cabins, storage rooms, and other equipment.

Construction and Boat Price Total 1 Million 138

The cost of the boat and the purchase of attached equipment is estimated at 44,000 pounds for the boat price, 1,300 pounds for fishing gear, 850 pounds for miscellaneous equipment and expenses, 1,450 pounds for testing and research equipment, microscopes, analytical instruments, medicine flow recorders, fish oil manufacturing machines, artificial drying machines, cameras, portable generators, diving suits, etc., 800 pounds for the travel expenses and salaries of special commissioners, and 1,600 pounds for repair costs (it is heard that various expenses have now been increased, totaling approximately 1 million yuan).

To be Implemented Upon Approval by the Gengkuan [Boxer Indemnity Funds] Committee 139

Mr. Chen's plan includes very detailed annual income and expenditure budgets, surplus estimates, and annual principal and interest repayment methods. It is now known that He Yushu, the head of the Guidance Huai River Committee, and others jointly designed it, and it has been approved by Chairman Chiang. It can be implemented once it is approved by the Gengkuan Committee. It is expected to be applicable by the autumn fishing season next year.

Report from the Salt Affairs Audit General Office on the Case of Tax Police Shooting Salt Farmers in Changlu 140

Tragic Incident of Destroying Saltpeter Ponds

The Police Sergeant Responsible Has Been Taken into Custody

According to Datong News Agency, the case of tax police in Changlu shooting salt farmers in Daming has attracted considerable attention from various parties. Yesterday, the Salt Affairs Audit General Office received a memorial from Zeng Yangfeng, the Changlu Salt Commissioner, reporting on the circumstances of the incident. Datong News Agency reporters have investigated the situation from all sides as follows:

Report from the Tax Police Side 141

The Salt Affairs Audit General Office received a report yesterday from Zeng Yangfeng, the Changlu Salt Commissioner, stating that according to a telegram from Inspector Li Peien and Zhang Ziying, the chief of the 8th district tax police, on the morning of the 8th, while leading a team and local militia police in the area of Zhao Gu Village in Daming, they were suddenly attacked by thousands of saltpeter bandits firing guns. Despite the efforts of Cheng, the head of the Bao Wei Tuan [Self-Defense Corps], and the head of the Public Security Bureau to persuade them, the bandits demanded that the tax police disarm or leave Deputy Yang to be dealt with by the saltpeter farmers. At that time, the crowd of bandits was closing in, and many police officers were injured, leaving them no choice but to return fire in self-defense, killing and wounding more than ten bandits on the spot and seizing five red-tasseled spears. The matter is currently under investigation.

Telegram from the Daming County Magistrate 142

In addition, according to a telegram from the Daming County Magistrate, tax police leveled salt ponds and have been convening village chiefs for days to persuade the people, ordering the police and militia to assist in the process, which was progressing smoothly. Unexpectedly, on the Geng day (8th) at 2:00 PM, there was a gathering of people in Zhao Gu and other villages. The tax police opened fire, and the people scattered. The county magistrate personally went to the scene to investigate and found twelve dead and thirteen wounded. The county magistrate is currently dividing his efforts to persuade and handle the aftermath. The office has ordered the chief of the tax police bureau to rush to the scene to investigate and handle the matter impartially.

Custody of the Police Sergeant Involved 143

According to inquiries made by reporters from related parties, after receiving the above telegram, Zeng Yangfeng, the Changlu Salt Commissioner, immediately dispatched Zhang Zhongli, the chief of the tax police bureau, to conduct an on-the-spot investigation and consult with County Magistrate Cheng on the aftermath. He also placed Yang Yi, the police sergeant who opened fire, under custody. However, the public believes that the tax police shot and killed dozens of salt farmers, causing an unprecedented tragedy. Public sentiment is very tense. After County Magistrate Cheng persuaded the people and promised to provide compensation to the deceased, the situation has eased.

Plan to Destroy Saltpeter Ponds 144

According to those familiar with the salt affairs, the Changlu Yamen's [government office] implementation of the plan to destroy saltpeter ponds was jointly decided by both the yamen and the office beforehand. The measures are briefly described as follows: (1) In the southwestern counties of Hebei Province, where the land is barren and the people are poor, permission has been obtained to reduce the salt tax by one yuan per dan [unit of weight] to ease the burden and combat private sales. (2) Special tax police squads are organized, together with local police and militia, as well as commercial patrols, to form a mixed destruction team to destroy privately established saltpeter ponds in various counties. (3) Measures are drafted for local officials to assist in promoting the sale of official salt and investigating and punishing saltpeter, in order to promote cooperation.

Zeng's Hasty Actions Lead to Change 145

According to another point of view, the Changlu Yamen's implementation of the plan to destroy saltpeter ponds, which concerns the people's food and the nation's tax revenue, is indeed a legitimate measure. However, the Changlu Salt Commissioner, Zeng Yangfeng, and the tax police personnel acted hastily, leading to a major tragedy, which was a mishandling of the situation and cannot be excused. It is also said that the General Office also attaches great importance to this case and will investigate it thoroughly.

Shanghai Municipal Council Agrees to Increase the General Hotel Tax in Three Stages 146

But the Hotel Industry Still Expresses Dissatisfaction

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the case of the Shanghai Municipal Council in the Public Concession increasing the winter police tax on the hotel industry has not yet been resolved despite appeals from the Hotel Association to various sectors. The seven hotels that the Municipal Council plans to increase the tax on, including Da Zhonghua, Dongfang, Xin Shijie, Jue Lu, Wu Gong, Da Shanghai, and Hui Zhong, have successively sent the taxes they should pay, but they have been rejected. The hotels believe that with the depression in all industries, it is difficult to comply with the increased tax. Therefore, they are determined to oppose it. The Hotel Industry previously asked Yu Qiaqing to mediate. Mr. Yu contacted Mr. Bourne, the head of the tax department of the Municipal Council. Mr. Bourne stated that he would change the method of increasing the tax and increase it in three stages according to the original tax amount: the first stage is an increase of one-quarter, the second stage is an increase of one-half, and the third stage is a full increase. However, the Hotel Industry is still firmly opposed to this.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Writes to Freight Truck Industry to Maintain Order and Await Resolution 147

And Submits a Petition to the Municipal Government for Consideration

The freight truck industry in this city has voluntarily suspended business due to its inability to bear the vehicle tax, and has requested the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for assistance. The Chamber of Commerce has now forwarded a petition to the Municipal Government, requesting consideration, and has also replied to the industry, urging it to maintain order. The letter is recorded as follows:

Document Submitted to the Municipal Government: A report respectfully requesting consideration of the facts. On the 16th of this month, the Freight Truck Industry Association stated in a letter that its members are facing the approaching winter license renewal period, and the case has not been resolved. Therefore, they have unanimously suspended business from today (the 15th) to seek the final understanding of the municipal authorities. The association, witnessing the difficult times, lacks the means to remedy the situation. In accordance with the resolution of the general meeting, it has instructed the representatives of each district to persuade members during the suspension to avoid unexpected disturbances and to maintain order while awaiting resolution. The suspension of business is a matter of great importance, and if it is prolonged, it will inevitably affect various industries and cause social panic. Therefore, it is forced to send a letter to your association to be forwarded to the Municipal Government, respectfully requesting the following points: (1) Please revise the original vehicle tax proposal. (2) Before the revision, winter licenses should be paid temporarily according to the autumn tax amount. (3) The case of requiring insurance for third parties this season to be approved for license issuance should be handled in the same way as the rental car industry, by paying a deposit to obtain a license. It is hoped that the matter will be reviewed and approved, in the interest of public welfare. The association has investigated the reasons for requesting exemption from the increased vehicle tax, and the aforementioned public association has previously presented various differences between freight trucks and private passenger cars, and the reasons for not increasing the tax are still valid. The situation in this case is now extremely tense, and if a solution is not sought quickly, it is feared that it will lead to unexpected events and affect society. In addition to sending a letter to the public association strictly ordering members to maintain order and await resolution, it is appropriate to submit a report to your government for review and approval, to show consideration and avoid causing incidents, which would be in the public interest.

Reply to the Industry: Directly replying, on the 16th of this month, we received a letter regarding the case of requesting exemption from the increased vehicle tax, which was not understood by the authorities. The industry has unanimously suspended business and put forward three requirements, requesting that they be forwarded to the Municipal Government for adoption. The Shanghai Municipal Government has already been informed of the situation. Your association is requested to restrain its members, maintain order, and await resolution. This is of utmost importance.

Implementing the Preliminary Plan for 22 Villages 152

Starting the Indigenous Cloth Revitalization Movement in Xianshan

Shao Shuangqiu, Dean of the College of Education at Great China University, recently planned to build the 22 Villages project, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. The reporter has recently learned more about its organizational plan and outline of teaching methods, which are disclosed below:

(Organization of Personnel) It will be jointly organized by a number of students from the College of Education of the university, a number of indigenous goods experts, a number of those with elementary school education experience, and a number of local district chiefs and farmers with qualifications.

(Establishment of Venues) Preliminary work will focus on the cotton weaving area of Xu Jiazhai, the planting area of Zhou Jiaqiao, Du Jiazhai, and Jin Jiaxiang, the rattan craft area, the consumer cooperative of Gui Lane, and the experimental elementary school of Mei Yuan. We will do our best to introduce indigenous cloth to restore the economic capacity of local residents, as a preparation for building new villages.

(Teaching Methods) As for teaching methods, each district will be guided by the district chief of that district every day. The district chief will be a student from the Education Department of Daxia University, or another expert hired. All residents in the district, regardless of age, must send someone to attend the class. If there are too many people, the characters will be written on the blackboard. If there are few, they will be replaced with scattered pieces of paper. Each person must learn ten or five characters per day until they can be applied. Then, they will be taught various techniques. The raw materials purchased by the cooperative from the countryside will be distributed to the members for use. After the members receive the raw materials, they must make them into finished products. After completion, they will be handed over to the district chief for safekeeping and re-receiving newly purchased goods for use.

(Improvement of Products) The textiles, which were originally pure white, have now been changed to use patterns and various flowers for easy sale. Recently, the society has also felt that indigenous goods are not thriving and the market is flooded with imported goods. In order to reverse the trend, it is necessary to implement the widespread use of indigenous goods. For the sake of practicality, it is planned to hold a large-scale indigenous goods movement week and establish indigenous goods production cooperatives, cooperative banks, textile training centers, and rural small handicraft training centers to realize the large-scale 22 New Villages.

A Skeleton Found at a Workshop 161

No Flesh Remaining, Only White Bones

Truth Unclear, Investigation Underway

According to the National News Agency, Dong Zhaoqian, the director of the Tangqiao Police Station in Pudong, under the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, received a report from Shi Bingsheng, the chief of the Bailianjing Police Station, stating that yesterday afternoon around 5 PM, Cao Changgen, a resident of 103 Bailianjing Street for generations, came to the station to report, "I have a house rented to the Ding Kang Yuan Sauce Garden. I recently heard from a rag-picking child that a corpse was discovered under the floor of the workshop area of the Ding Kang Yuan Sauce Garden. I am reporting this matter for investigation and verification." After verifying the report, Director Dong immediately went to investigate and found that behind the house at 161 Bailianjing, next to the riverbank, there was indeed a long-dead corpse under the floor. All the flesh was gone, leaving only a complete skeleton. Director Dong then ordered Cao Changgen to be brought in for questioning. Cao testified that he runs a tofu shop on this street and that the house was built around 1926 on the Bailianjing beach. There are three single-story houses in total, with two house numbers, 159 and 161. In 1930, he rented house number 161 to Chen Er, a native of Nanhui County, to use as a pig slaughtering workshop. In April 1933, the Chen family rented it to the Ding Kang Yuan Sauce Garden for business. In November of the same year, he rented house number 161 to the Ding Kang Yuan Sauce Garden as a workshop. It was not until 5 PM on the 14th of this month that he heard from a rag-picking child about the discovery of the corpse, hence his report to the police station. He further summoned Li Houyu, the owner of the Ding Kang Yuan Sauce Garden, who stated that the sauce garden had rented the house as a workshop for only a few months and knew nothing about the corpse under the floor. After hearing the testimony, Director Dong ordered Chen Baoming, the local headman, to report to the court for a coroner's examination. He also ordered the landlord, Cao Changgen, to be temporarily released on bail, pending further investigation. Meanwhile, he dispatched officers to investigate the details and await the court's examination to clarify the truth.

Li Yingchang and Others Convicted in Counterfeit Currency Case 162

Sentenced to Eight Years, Five Months, Six Months, and One Year Respectively

Li Yingchang, a 40-year-old Yunnan native residing in the pavilion room on the third floor of Hengchang Lane, 3 Beile Road in the French Concession, recently entrusted Liu Guangsheng, a 29-year-old Danyang native who runs a printing business at 24 Zhicheng Lane, Lanwei Avenue in Shanghai, to privately print counterfeit banknotes of the Yunnan Fudian New Bank, each worth 50 copper cents, with the intention of transporting them to Yunnan for circulation. At 12 PM on the 12th of last month, Li placed a receipt book with a square hole cut out in the center and filled it with the counterfeit banknotes, intending to mail them to Yunnan as samples. However, he was apprehended at the entrance of Hengchang Lane by Detective Chief Jin Jiulin of the French Police and detectives Zhou Buguang, Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, and others during a patrol. They arrested both Cai and Liu and confiscated 20,500 identical counterfeit banknotes and related correspondence from Cai's house. They also found printing machine models at 71 La Fayette Road, which Liu had rented. It was further discovered that Ji Jinquan, a local resident living at 43 Yongyu Lane, Beile Road, had been acting as an intermediary for Cai Yingchang, receiving and forwarding letters. Consequently, Cai was also arrested and sent to the Second Special District Court for investigation. Subsequent investigation of the letters seized from Cai's house revealed an agreement with Cai Xinmin in Yunnan, whereby Cai Xinmin would send morphine hidden in letters to Shanghai for Cai to sell, and Cai would send counterfeit banknotes to Yunnan for Cai Xinmin to circulate and sell. These letters were received and forwarded by Ji Jinquan. The details of the report to the court and the subsequent investigation have been previously published. The trial has now concluded, and yesterday morning, Judge Cao Jun presided over the first criminal court session and sentenced Li Yingchang to eight years of imprisonment, a fine of 600 yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for ten years. Liu Guangsheng was sentenced to five years and six months of imprisonment, a fine of 200 yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for ten years. Ji Jinquan was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 300 yuan. The counterfeit banknotes and related correspondence were confiscated.

Nine Seamen Arrested from the President Jefferson 165

The Greater American Newspaper reports that when the President Jefferson, a mail ship of the Dollar Steamship Lines, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon (the 16th), agents of the US Consular Police, along with the water police, boarded the ship at the Dollar Wharf and arrested seven seamen from the engine room. This was based on a wireless message sent by Captain Rustad, stating that on October 12th, three hours after the ship departed Yokohama for Shanghai, two seamen were attacked by seamen from the engine room. One was hit in the head with a beer bottle and seriously injured, while the other was bitten. Therefore, yesterday, when the ship docked, none of the seamen were allowed to disembark. The two injured Englishmen identified the perpetrators, leading to the arrest of seven men, who were taken ashore and imprisoned at the Xiamen Road Western Jail. This morning (the 17th), after an investigation by the authorities, two more seamen from the ship were arrested. The case is currently under thorough investigation by the local prosecutor. It is expected that the court will hold a hearing this afternoon. The maximum penalty could be six months of imprisonment and a fine of 500 US dollars. The President Jefferson is scheduled to sail to Hong Kong and Manila tonight and will depart as scheduled. It is reported that replacements have been hired for the nine detained seamen.

Red Pill Case Sentenced Separately 173

Chen Aqing Sentenced to Four Years

Fine of 1,500 Yuan

At 5 AM on the 2nd of this month, West Inspector Lang Baile, Chinese Inspector Li Yaolong, Detective Zhang Daorong, and detectives Liu Jinrong and Shen Jinshi of the French Police were patrolling Xinkiao Street on Fa Da Road when they saw Zhu Renzu, from Wuxi, carrying three mooncake boxes and looking flustered. Upon searching, they found 3,000 red pills. Zhu confessed that he had bought them from Jin Cai, a local resident living in the pavilion room at 26 Baoxing Lane, Dongxinkiao Street. The detectives then took Zhu to Jin's residence and arrested him. They also found 8,000 red pills on the kitchen loft. Jin confessed that the red pills were delivered by Li Fengxiang, from Nanjing, who lived at 3 Baolong Lane, Huaizhen Street, Jiu Mu Di. The detectives then coordinated with detectives from the Public Security Bureau to arrest Li. Li confessed that he was hired by Chen Aqing, from Ningbo, who lived at 122 Baer Road, to deliver the red pills. The detectives then went to Baer Road and arrested Chen Aqing. Later, at 11 Xiaoyou Lane, 26 Luban Road, they uncovered a manufacturing operation and seized 5,000 red pills, along with baking ovens and manufacturing equipment. They also arrested Zhang Rongji and Zhang Chen, a couple from Ningbo who were employees of the operation, and transferred them to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. Details of these events were reported in the previous newspaper. After being interrogated by Wang Gangxu, the presiding judge of the criminal court, Chen Aqing was sentenced to four years of imprisonment and a fine of 1,500 yuan, Jin Cai was sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment and a fine of 500 yuan, Li Fengxiang was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment and a fine of 200 yuan, Zhu Renzu was sentenced to two years of imprisonment and a fine of 200 yuan, and Zhang Rongji and Zhang Chen were each fined 200 yuan. The number of days spent in detention before the judgment was determined would be used to offset the imprisonment by two days for each day of detention. If the fines were commuted to imprisonment, Chen Aqing's total fine would be converted to imprisonment at a ratio of one day for the total fine amount, and the remainder would be converted to imprisonment at a ratio of two yuan for each day of imprisonment. The red pill equipment, and other items in the case would be confiscated and destroyed.

Factory Girl Seduced, Awaiting Sentencing 174

Sun Qiyu, a 17-year-old girl named Xiao Erzi, who resides in a bungalow on Meizhou Road and is from Funing, has been working in the spinning room of the Zhenhua Cotton Mill on the same road. She has an ordinary appearance. Recently, she fell in love with Zhang Yongfang, a worker at the Huitong Cotton Mill on Lan Road, and they are very close. On the evening of the 13th of this month, Zhang took Sun to live with him at 679 Yangshupu Road. At 4 PM the next day, her father, Sun Qiyu, found out and reported it to the Yangshupu Police Station. Detective Guo Jingbang and a Western detective secretly went to the address and arrested Zhang, along with Sun Xiao Erzi, and brought them to the police station for delivery to the First Special District Court. The daughter said that she was 21 years old and willing to marry Zhang Yongfang. She firmly refused to go home with her father. She was instructed to be temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute pending verification of her age. The defendant was returned to custody. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan presided over the continued trial in the third criminal court. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Shanghai Municipal Council, stated that the police had sent detectives to the spinning department of the Zhenhua Factory and found that worker ID number 723 belonged to Wang Xiuying, a woman from Yangzhou, who was 19 years old. The age, origin, and name of the Sun girl did not match. Sun Xiao Erzi insisted that she was 21 years old and that Wang Xiuying's ID was her alias. She admitted to having reported two years less at the time. According to her father, Sun Qiyu, his daughter was 17 years old and had been promised to a Mr. So-and-so from her hometown as a daughter-in-law. When questioned, the defendant confessed that the matter was entirely Sun Xiao Erzi's own will. He had previously sent a matchmaker to the Sun family to arrange the marriage, but her mother did not agree because she wanted a certain amount of betrothal money, which he could not afford. Sun Xiao Erzi was afraid of being beaten by her parents and still refused to return home. Judge Wu gave the girl a sincere lecture and instructed her father not to beat her too harshly. He then instructed that the defendant be held in custody pending a scheduled sentence, and Sun Xiao Erzi was released to Sun Qiyu to be taken home.

Destitution Leads to Attempted Suicide in Huangpu River 176

Rescued and Revived

At around 6 AM yesterday, a middle-aged man was seen pacing back and forth at the Customs Wharf on Hankou Road, appearing deeply troubled. However, no one paid attention at the time. Suddenly, the man jumped into the Huangpu River in an attempt to commit suicide. Fortunately, a guard spotted him and quickly summoned a sampan boat parked near the wharf to pull him out of the water and onto the wharf. He reported the incident to the police, who transported him to the hospital for treatment. Fortunately, he had not ingested much water, so he was revived after emergency treatment. When asked for his name, he said that his name was Wang Hexu, from Shaoxing, and that he was taking this drastic measure due to destitution.

Letters 192

To the Editor: On October 15th, I saw a news item in your newspaper titled "Penalties for Smuggling Cigarettes," which is not in accordance with the facts. The Jingzhong brand cigarettes of Qiu Mingde's Shanghai Ningtai Qiaji Cigarette Company are manufactured by our factory. The raw materials, tobacco, casings, trademarks, paper, etc., are entirely provided and used by the company. At the time of delivery, our factory staff, together with the tax bureau's stationed committee member, supervise the packing and affix the tax stamps before leaving the factory for sale. The repacking of old-label waxed paper-wrapped cigarettes is impossible. Moreover, the cigarettes seized were all in the home of Qiu Mingde of Ningtai Company. I was not present at the time, and there was no bringing to the police station or transferring to the court. According to Qiu Mingde's testimony in court, the smuggled loose cigarettes were accumulated by repeatedly requesting loose cigarettes from the Donghai Cigarette Factory for his own use and as samples. He was greedy for small profits and secretly repacked them at home with old waxed paper and sold them on the market. The Donghai Cigarette Factory was completely unaware of this. According to everything Qiu Mingde said, the case is unrelated to our factory and is completely clear. Our factory has been open for ten years and has never engaged in illegal private manufacturing. This time, Qiu Mingde of Ningtai Company committed a violation of the tax bureau's regulations, which implicated our factory and my reputation, which is detestable. We have stopped manufacturing for them. As for the loose cigarettes of Qiu Mingde, according to his testimony in court, they were accumulated by repeatedly requesting them from our factory. This point may also not be in accordance with the facts. Although we can request some for our own use or as samples, it would only be one or two hundred. It is impossible to take an unlimited amount, but there were more than 100 strips or 28,000 cigarettes seized in Qiu Mingde's home. It is possible that he manufactured them privately, otherwise, even if accumulated, there would not be such a huge number. In the interest of reputation, I am writing to request verification and correction to avoid misunderstanding. Sincerely, Shi Shenkang, Donghai Cigarette Factory, October 17th.
